The framework consists of several key components:\\n\\n## Migration Runner (migrator.go)\\nThe `Migrator` struct in `migrator.go` is the core runner that orchestrates database migrations. Key features include:\\n- `RunMigrations()` method: Main entry point that manages database locking and initiates the migration process\\n- `run()` method: Executes all pending migrations and handles (sqlite_dialect.go): SQLite-specific implementations with different autoincrement syntax\\n\\nThe `BaseDialect` class provides common implementations that all dialects inherit from, including standard SQL generation methods.\\n\\n## Migration Rollback Handling (migrator.go)\\nRollback handling is implemented through:\\n- `InTransaction()` method: Wraps migration execution in database transactions\\n- Calls `sess.Begin()` to start a transaction, `sess.Commit()` on success, and `sess.Rollback()` on error\\n- The migration execution methods (`doMigration()`, `exec()`) are called within transactional context\\n- Failed migrations are automatically rolled back, and the error is recorded in the migration log\\n- Database locking is also handled transactionally using advisory locks (for MySQL/PostgreSQL)\\n\\n## Migration Types and Conditions\\nThe framework supports various migration types defined in `migrations.go`:\\n- `RawSQLMigration`: Direct SQL execution with dialect-specific SQL variants\\n- `AddColumnMigration`, `AddTableMigration`, `DropTableMigration`: DDL operations\\n- `RenameColumnMigration`, `RenameTableMigration`: Deprecated operations for already-applied migrations\\n\\nThe `Column` type (column.go) and `Table`, `Index` types (types.go) provide the data structures for defining database schema The framework consists of several key components:\\n\\n## Migration Runner (migrator.go)\\nThe `Migrator` struct in `migrator.go` is the core runner that orchestrates database migrations. Key features include:\\n- `RunMigrations()` method: Main entry point that manages database locking and initiates the migration process\\n- `run()` method: Executes all pending migrations and handles the migration log\\n- `doMigration()` method: Executes individual migrations with transactional support\\n- `exec()` method: Evaluates migration conditions and executes the SQL or code migrations\\n\\n## Migration Version Tracking Table (migrator.go)\\nThe `MigrationLog` struct in `migrator.go` defines the version tracking table structure:\\n- Stores `MigrationID`, `SQL`, `Success`, `Error`, and `Timestamp` for each migration\\n- Created automatically via `AddCreateMigration()` method which creates the `migration_log` table\\n- `GetMigrationLog()` method retrieves the list of already-executed migrations\\n- The framework tracks which migrations have been executed to avoid re-running them\\n\\n## SQL Dialect Abstraction (dialect.go and dialect implementations)\\nThe `Dialect` interface in `dialect.go` provides a database-agnostic abstraction with methods for:\\n- Creating/modifying tables, columns, and indexes\\n- Dialect-specific SQL generation (CreateTableSQL, AddColumnSQL, etc.)\\n- Error handling and detection\\n- Database locking mechanisms (Lock/Unlock methods)\\n\\nSpecific dialect implementations:\\n- `MySQLDialect` (mysql_dialect.go): MySQL-specific implementations with engine support and custom error handling\\n- `PostgresDialect` (postgres_dialect.go): PostgreSQL-specific implementations with case-insensitive LIKE operators\\n- `SQLite3` (sqlite_dialect.go): SQLite-specific implementations with different autoincrement syntax\\n\\nThe `BaseDialect` class provides common implementations that all dialects inherit from, including standard SQL generation methods.\\n\\n## Migration Rollback Handling (migrator.go)\\nRollback handling is implemented through:\\n- `InTransaction()` method: Wraps migration execution in database transactions\\n- Calls `sess.Begin()` to start a transaction, `sess.Commit()` on success, and `sess.Rollback()` on error\\n- The migration execution methods (`doMigration()`, `exec()`) are called within transactional context\\n- Failed migrations are automatically rolled back, and the error is recorded in the migration log\\n- Database locking is also handled transactionally using advisory locks (for MySQL/PostgreSQL)\\n\\n## Migration Types and Conditions\\nThe framework supports various migration types defined in `migrations.go`:\\n- `RawSQLMigration`: Direct SQL execution with dialect-specific SQL variants\\n- `AddColumnMigration`, `AddTableMigration`, `DropTableMigration`: DDL operations\\n- `RenameColumnMigration`, `RenameTableMigration`: Deprecated operations for backward compatibility\\n- `AddIndexMigration`, `DropIndexMigration`: Index management\\n\\nConditional execution is supported via `MigrationCondition` interface in `conditions.go`:\\n- `IfColumnNotExistsCondition`: Only execute if column doesn't exist\\n- `IfIndexExistsCondition`/`IfIndexNotExistsCondition`: Index-based conditions\\n- These conditions prevent re-execution of already-applied migrations\\n\\nThe `Column` type (column.go) and `Table`, `Index` types (types.go) provide the data structures for defining database schema changes.\"\n    49→}\n
